The Ruling on Prostrating on the Edge of the Turban
Ruling on prostrating on the edge of the turban

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prostrating on the edge of the turban and identify the exception for necessity.

Core Idea
Prostrating on the turban's edge is mildly disliked unless excused by heat, cold, or rough ground.

This lesson examines the ruling on prostrating while the edge of the turban (kawr al-'imamah) contacts the ground instead of the forehead directly. The Hanafi school considers this action makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked) because it compromises the full humility of prostration. However, the disliked status is lifted when there is a genuine excuse, such as extreme temperatures or uneven terrain. We will explore the textual evidence and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is prostrating on the edge (kawr) of the turban. The ruling is makruh tanzih (mildly disliked).
2
Understand the reason for the ruling
The dislike stems from the lack of complete khushu' (humility) since the forehead is not directly placed on the ground.
3
Examine the proof
A weak hadith in Marasil Abi Dawud shows the Prophet removing a turban from a man's forehead during prayer, indicating the importance of direct forehead contact.
4
Identify the exception
If there is a necessity like extreme heat, cold, or rough ground, it is not disliked.
5
Distinguish between the edge and the main part
The ruling applies only to the edge; prostrating on the main body of the turban is not disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسُّجُودُ على كَوْرِ عِمامتِه، [٣]قوله : والسجود على كَوْرِ عمامته ؛ العمامة بالكسر ما يعتم به على الرأس ، بالفارسية : دستار، وكل دورة منها يسمّى كوراً بالفتح ، بالفارسية: تريج دستار، قال في «البحر»: «الظاهر أنّ الكراهة تنزيهية لنقل فعله الله وأصحابه من السجودِ على كَوْرِ (٠) العمامة تعليماً للجواز». (انتهى) وفي «مراقي الفلاح»: «إن كان لعذر كدفع الحر والبرد وخشونة الأرض لا يكره ، وإلا يكره». انتهى ) . ووجه الكراهة : أنّ فيه ترك كمال الخضوع، فإنّه في إلصاق الجبهة بالأرض، ويؤيده ما روى أبو داود في «مراسيله» بسند ضعيف: «أنّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى رجلاً يصلي وقد اعتم على جبهته، فحسر رسول الله عن جبهته).
And prostrating on the edge of his turban. [3] His statement: 'and prostrating on the edge of his turban': The turban (with kasr) is what is wound on the head; in Persian: dastar. Each fold is called a kawr (with fatha); in Persian: terij-e dastar. He said in al-Bahr: 'It appears that the dislike is tanzihi because its action was transmitted from Allah and His companions prostrating on the edge of the turban to teach permissibility.' (end) And in Maraqi al-Falah: 'If it is for an excuse such as repelling heat, cold, or roughness of the ground, it is not disliked; otherwise it is disliked.' (end) The reason for the dislike is that it involves abandoning complete humility, which is in pressing the forehead to the ground. This is supported by what Abu Dawud narrated in his Marasil with a weak chain: 'The Messenger of Allah saw a man praying with his turban wrapped on his forehead, so he removed it from his forehead.'
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on prostrating on the edge (kawr) of the turban. The commentator explains the meaning of turban and edge. The ruling is that it is makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked) unless there is an excuse like heat, cold, or rough ground. The proof is from actions of the Prophet and companions, and a marfu' hadith (although weak) where the Prophet removed a turban from a man's forehead during prostration. The reason for the dislike is that it prevents full humility by not directly pressing the forehead to the ground.

Key Terms
كور العمامة (kawr al-'imamah): The folded edge or top part of the turban that touches the ground during prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Prostrating on the edge of the turban is mildly disliked in Hanafi fiqh unless a valid excuse exists, emphasizing direct forehead contact for full humility.

The Ruling on Counting Verses and Tasbih in Prayer
Definition and ruling on counting verses or tasbih in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on counting verses or tasbih during prayer and explain why it is considered makruh tanzih.

Core Idea
Counting in prayer distracts from khushu — the Hanafi school considers it makruh tanzih.

This passage addresses a common question: Is it permissible to count the number of verses or tasbih while praying? The Hanafi position is clear: such counting is disliked (makruh tanzih) because it diverts the mind from the essence of prayer. Let us examine the ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is counting the number of Qur'anic verses (ayi) or tasbih phrases (e.g., 'Subhanallah') during salah. The Hanafi ruling is that it is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked).
The ruling applies to both mental counting and finger counting.
2
Define the key terms
'Ay' is the plural of 'ayah', meaning verses of the Qur'an. 'Tasbih' refers to phrases like 'Subhanallah'. 'Al-'add' means counting, with emphasis on the act of enumerating.
Understanding the terms helps grasp the scope of the ruling.
3
Understand the underlying principle
Prayer requires khushu (full focus and humility). Counting divides the mind, reducing khushu. Hence, it is disliked.
The principle is maintaining the spirit of worship.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some scholars allow counting if it helps avoid errors in recitation. The Hanafi school prioritizes avoiding distraction over the benefit of accuracy.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different assessments of what breaks khushu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعد الآي والتسبيح فيها، [٤]قوله : وعد الآي...الخ ; الآي بالمد: جمع آية، والعد بفتح العين وتشديد
And counting the verses and tasbih in it. [4] His statement: 'and counting the verses...' The al-ay (with madd) is plural of ayah, and al-'add (with fatha of the 'ayn and tashdid) ...
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on counting verses (ayi) and tasbih (subhanallah etc.) during prayer. The commentator defines the terms: 'ayi' is plural of 'ayah' (verse), and 'al-'add' means counting with emphasis. The ruling is that such counting is disliked because it involves mental activity distracting from focus in prayer. No explicit proof is given in the available text, but it is based on the principle of maintaining khushu.

Key Terms
عد الآي (add al-ayi): Counting the number of verses recited during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does 'عد الآي' mean in the context of prayer?
A) Reciting verses quickly
B) Counting the number of verses recited
C) Repeating verses
D) Memorizing verses

Key Takeaway
Counting verses or tasbih in prayer is makruh tanzih because it distracts from khushu.

Ruling on Wiping Dust During Prayer: The Hadith and Its Interpretation
Ruling with hadith on wiping dust during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping dust from the forehead during prayer and explain the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah) from the hadith.

Core Idea
Wiping dust during prayer is not haram, but makruh tanzih — the prohibition is interpreted as dislike to preserve focus.

In this lesson, we examine a specific action within prayer: wiping the forehead to remove dust. The Prophet (peace be upon him) gave a clear instruction, but how is it understood in the Hanafi school? We will see that not every prohibition implies unlawfulness; sometimes it indicates dislike to maintain khushu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping the forehead from dust during prayer. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked, not forbidden).
2
Locate the hadith proof
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not wipe pebbles while you are praying.' By analogy, wiping dust from the forehead is included.
The hadith is narrated by the six major collections.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative prohibition (la tamsah) is understood as karahah because it is not a definitive prohibition (nahi muhattam); the aim is to avoid distraction.
The hadith is ahad, so its authority is zanni, and the ruling is accordingly mild.
4
Note the consensus
The ruling is agreed upon among the major schools (muttafaq alayh); there is no significant dispute.
This strengthens the Hanafi position.
5
Apply the ruling practically
In practice, one should refrain from such wiping during prayer; after the prayer, it is permissible.
If dust is excessive and distracting, a light wipe may be excused, but preferably avoided.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومسح جبهته من التراب فيها.
[1] قوله : ومسح جبهته ؛ قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا تمسح الحصى وأنت تصلي (1) أخرجه أصحاب الكتب الستة.
(1) فعن أبي ذره قال : إذا قام أحدكم إلى الصلاة فلا يمسح الحصى، فإن الرحمة تواجهه» في سنن الترمذي (۲ : ۲۱۹)، وسنن أبي داود»(۱ : ۳۱۲)، وغيرها.
And wiping his forehead from dust in it. [1] His statement: and wiping his forehead; the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not wipe pebbles while you are praying' (1) reported by the authors of the six books. (1) From Abu Dharr who said: 'When one of you stands for prayer, let him not wipe pebbles, for mercy faces him' in Sunan al-Tirmidhi (2:219), Sunan Abi Dawud (1:312), etc.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school: wiping the forehead from dust during prayer is makruh (disliked). The proof is a hadith narrated by the six major hadith collections: the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited wiping pebbles while praying. This includes dust on the forehead as a form of removing dirt. The prohibition indicates karahah (dislike) not tahrim (unlawfulness) because it distracts from khushu' and is not part of the prayer actions. The footnote provides an alternate narration emphasizing that one should not wipe the ground.

Key Terms
مسح (masah): wiping, removing something with the hand
حصى (hasah): pebbles, small stones (used in the hadith)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on wiping the forehead from dust during prayer according to this passage?
A) Haram
B) Makruh
C) Wajib
D) Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Wiping dust from the forehead during prayer is disliked (makruh) because it distracts from the prayer's focus, based on the Prophet's command to avoid unnecessary movement.

Ruling on Looking Up to the Sky in Prayer
Ruling with hadith on looking up

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking up to the sky in prayer, identify the hadith proof, and explain why it is makruh tanzih rather than haram.

Core Idea
Looking up to the sky in prayer is makruh tanzih because it violates khushu'.

In this lesson, we examine a specific act that undermines the spirit of prayer: looking up to the sky. The Hanafi school, based on a strong Prophetic warning, classifies this as makruh tanzih (disliked). Understanding this ruling helps preserve the humility (khushu') required in salah and clarifies the legal weight of the hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, note the act under discussion: looking up to the sky during prayer. The ruling given is that it is makruh (disliked). Identify the specific level: makruh tanzih.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked, 'What is the matter with people who raise their eyes to the sky in their prayer?' and warned, 'They must refrain from that or their eyesight will be snatched away.' This hadith is reported by Bukhari, Muslim, and others.
The hadith is authentic (sahih) but ahad.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The severe threat (loss of eyesight) indicates strong prohibition. However, the Hanafi school interprets this threat as metaphorical or conditional, not absolute, so the ruling is karahah (dislike) not haram.
The threat is zanni in dalala.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Check if there is disagreement. In this case, the ruling is muttafaq alayh – all schools agree looking up is disliked. However, some may consider it makruh tahrimi (close to haram) due to the threat. The Hanafis opt for tanzih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi: makruh tanzih. This is based on the principle that ahad hadith with zanni dalala cannot establish absolute prohibition, and because the act does not invalidate prayer.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنظر إلى السماء.
[2] قوله : والنظر إلى السماء ؛ لأنَّ فيه ترك الخشوع وسوء الأدب، وقد قال النبي : ما بال أقوام يرفعون أبصارهم إلى السماء في صلاتهم»)، وقال: «لينتهنّ عن ذلك أو لتخطفن أبصارهم» (3) ، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم ، وأبو داود وغيرهم بألفاظ متقاربة.
(3) في «صحيح البخاري»(١ : ٢٦١)، وغيره.
And looking up to the sky. [2] His statement: and looking up to the sky; because it involves leaving humility and bad manners, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'What is the matter with people who raise their eyes to the sky in their prayer?' and said: 'They must refrain from that or their eyesight will be snatched away' (3), reported by Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud and others with similar wording. (3) In Sahih al-Bukhari (1:261), etc.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling: looking up to the sky during prayer is makruh because it contradicts khushu' (humility) and is bad etiquette. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) strongly warned against raising eyes to the sky, threatening loss of eyesight. This indicates karahah tahrimi (reprehensible close to forbidden) or tanzih depending on context, but the Hanafi school generally considers it makruh tanzih. The hadith is authentic, reported by Bukhari and Muslim.

Key Terms
الخشوع (al-khushu'): humility and attentiveness in prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is looking up to the sky during prayer disliked?
A) It invalidates prayer
B) It is a form of arrogance
C) It contradicts humility (khushu')
D) It is forbidden

Key Takeaway
Looking up to the sky in prayer is makruh tanzih due to the Prophetic warning and its contradiction of khushu'.

Prostrating on the Fold of the Turban: Humility and Excuses
Ruling on prostrating on turban fold with evidence and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prostrating on the turban fold and identify when it is permissible due to an excuse.

Core Idea
Prostrating on the turban fold is makruh tanzih unless an excuse prevents direct forehead contact.

In this passage, the author explains the ruling on prostrating on the fold of the turban. While it is generally disliked, the dislike is light (tanzih) and can be lifted when there is a genuine need. The evidence includes a weak hadith and the principle of humility in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is prostrating on the fold of the turban (kawr al-ʿimāmah). The default ruling is makruh tanzih (light dislike).
The ruling comes from later Hanafi works like al-Bahr and Marāqī al-Falāḥ.
2
Understand the reason for dislike
The dislike is because it prevents the forehead from directly touching the ground, reducing complete humility in prostration.
The weakness of the supporting hadith contributes to the dislike being tanzih rather than tahrimi.
3
Note the exception for excuses
When there is an excuse such as extreme heat, cold, or rough ground, the dislike is removed and it becomes permissible.
This is based on Marāqī al-Falāḥ and the principle of necessity.
4
Examine the evidence
The passage cites a weak hadith narrated by Abu Dawud where the Prophet uncovered a man's forehead during prayer. This indicates the preferred practice but is not strong enough to prohibit.
The hadith is weak (da'if), so it only supports dislike, not prohibition.
5
Recognize the authority sources
The ruling relies on al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq and Marāqī al-Falāḥ, which are authoritative later Hanafi texts (fatāwā muta'akhkhirīn).
This shows the evolution of the madhhab in dealing with weak evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسُّجُودُ على كَوْرِ عِمامتِه.
[3] قوله : والسجود على كَوْرِ عمامته ؛ العمامة بالكسر ما يعتم به على الرأس ، بالفارسية : دستار، وكل دورة منها يسمّى كوراً بالفتح ، بالفارسية: تريج دستار، قال في «البحر»: «الظاهر أنّ الكراهة تنزيهية لنقل فعله الله وأصحابه من السجودِ على كَوْرِ العمامة تعليماً للجواز». (انتهى) وفي «مراقي الفلاح»: «إن كان لعذر كدفع الحر والبرد وخشونة الأرض لا يكره ، وإلا يكره». انتهى ) . ووجه الكراهة : أنّ فيه ترك كمال الخضوع، فإنّه في إلصاق الجبهة بالأرض، ويؤيده ما روى أبو داود في «مراسيله» بسند ضعيف: «أنّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى رجلاً يصلي وقد اعتم على جبهته، فحسر رسول الله عن جبهته).
(4) من البحر الرائق» (۲ : ۳۳۷).
(5) من «مراقي الفلاح» (ص ۳۳۷).
(6) في مراسيل أبي داود (۱) : (١٠٤) ، و(السنن الصغرى (۱) : (٣٥٥) ، و(سنن البيهقي الكبير» (٢ : ١٠٥)، وغيرها.
And prostrating on the fold of his turban. [3] His statement: and prostrating on the fold of his turban; the turban (al-ʿimāmah) is what one wraps on the head, in Persian: dastār, and each turn of it is called kawr (with fatha), in Persian: tarīj-i dastār. [Author] said in al-Bahr: 'It appears that the dislike is tanzih because the action of Allah and His companions of prostrating on the fold of the turban has been transmitted as teaching permissibility.' (End). And in Marāqī al-Falāḥ: 'If there is an excuse like heat, cold, or roughness of the ground, it is not disliked; otherwise it is disliked.' End. And the reason for dislike: that it involves leaving complete humility, because it is in attaching the forehead to the ground, and it is supported by what Abu Dawud narrated in his Marāsīl with a weak chain: 'That the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saw a man praying while wearing his turban on his forehead, so the Messenger of Allah uncovered his forehead.' (4) From al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq (2:337). (5) From Marāqī al-Falāḥ (p.337). (6) In Marāsīl Abī Dāwūd (1:104), al-Sunan al-Ṣughrā (1:355), Sunan al-Bayhaqī al-Kabīr (2:105), etc.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on prostrating on the fold of the turban (kawr al-ʿimāmah). The author explains that 'kawr' refers to each turn of the turban. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful), as stated in al-Bahr, because the action of the Prophet and his companions shows permissibility. However, if there is a valid excuse (heat, cold, rough ground), it is not disliked. The reason for dislike is that it prevents the forehead from directly touching the ground, thus reducing humility. A weak hadith supports this: the Prophet uncovered a man's forehead when he prayed with his turban on it. The footnotes provide sources.

Key Terms
كور العمامة (kawr al-ʿimāmah): the fold or turn of the turban

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is never disliked

Key Takeaway
Prostrating on the turban fold is makruh tanzih, but becomes permissible when there is a valid excuse such as heat, cold, or rough ground.

Ruling on Counting Verses and Tasbih in Prayer
Detailed ruling on counting with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and impermissible methods of counting during prayer and apply the Hanafi ruling on each.

Core Idea
Counting verses by hand is disliked; by tongue invalidates the prayer.

When you pray, do you ever catch yourself counting verses or tasbih with your fingers? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling: it depends on how you count. This lesson explores the detailed classification from the classical texts, highlighting the subtle differences between hand, tongue, and mental counting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the method of counting
Determine whether the person counts by hand (finger or thread), by tongue (speaking), or by pressing fingertips/mentally.
The ruling hinges on this distinction.
2
Determine the ruling for each method
For each method, recall the consensus or dispute: by hand is makruh tanzih, by tongue is mufsid, mentally is not disliked.
The passage explicitly states these rulings.
3
Distinguish between fard and nafl
Note that the dislike applies to both fard and nafl, though some scholars exempt nafl. Understand the scope of the ikhtilaf.
This is the intra-Hanafi dispute.
4
Apply the ruling outside prayer
Recognize that counting dhikr outside prayer, even with a rosary, is not disliked.
The context of prayer is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعد الآي والتسبيح فيها.
[4] قوله : وعد الآي...الخ ؛ الآي بالمد: جمع آية، والعد بفتح العين وتشديد الدال ، ذكر في «البحر» (1) و «الحلبة» و«البناية» وغيرها : أنّ محل الخلاف إنما هو العد باليد، سواء كان بأصبعه أو بخيط يمسكه، أما الغمز برؤوس الأصابع والحفظ بالقلب فلا يكره اتفاقاً، والعد باللسان مفسد اتفاقاً. وقيد بالآي والتسبيح ؛ لأنّ عد غيرهما مكروه اتفاقاً، والكراهة هاهنا تنزيهية ؛ لكونه ليس من أعمال الصلاة ومنافياً للخشوع، وفي الإطلاق إشارة إلى الكراهة في التطوع والمكتوبة كليهما ، وقيل : لا يكره في النوافل، وهذا كله في الصلاة، وأما عدا الأذكار خارجها فلا يكره، سواءً كان باليد أو بالسبحة، وقد فصلت الكلام على هذه المسائل في رسالتي نزهة الفكر في سبحة الذكر».
(1) «البحر الرائق» (۲ : ۳۱).
And counting verses and tasbih in it. [4] His statement: and counting verses... etc.; al-āy (with madd) is plural of āyah, and al-ʿadd (with fatha on ʿayn and shadda on dāl). It is mentioned in al-Bahr (1), al-Ḥalabah, al-Bināyah and others: the point of disagreement is only regarding counting by hand, whether with the finger or a thread he holds; as for pressing with fingertips and memorizing by heart, it is not disliked by consensus, and counting by tongue invalidates [prayer] by consensus. It is restricted to verses and tasbih because counting other than them is disliked by consensus, and the dislike here is tanzihi because it is not among the actions of prayer and contradicts khushu'. And in the absolute sense, it indicates dislike in both voluntary and obligatory prayers; and it is said: it is not disliked in nafl prayers. All this is within prayer, but as for counting dhikr outside prayer, it is not disliked, whether by hand or with a rosary. And I have detailed these issues in my treatise Nuzhat al-Fikr fī Sabḥat al-Dhikr. (1) Al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq (2:31).
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on counting verses and tasbih during prayer. It distinguishes between methods: counting by hand (finger or thread) is a point of ikhtilaf (disagreement) among scholars, but the relied-upon position is that it is makruh tanzih (disliked). Pressing fingertips or memorizing by heart is not disliked by consensus. Counting by tongue invalidates the prayer by consensus. The dislike is restricted to counting verses and tasbih; counting other things is disliked by consensus. The ruling applies to both fard and nafl prayers, though some say it is not disliked in nafl. Outside prayer, counting dhikr (even with a rosary) is not disliked. The author references other Hanafi works.

Key Terms
عد الآي (ʿadd al-āy): counting the verses of the Quran during prayer
تسبيح (tasbīḥ): saying SubhanAllah, usually repeated a specific number of times

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on counting verses by tongue during prayer?
A) Makruh tanzih
B) Makruh tahrimi
C) Invalidates prayer (mufsid)
D) Permissible

Key Takeaway
Counting by tongue invalidates prayer; by hand is makruh tanzih; pressing fingertips or mental counting is permissible.

Ruling on Wearing Garments with Images in Prayer
Ruling on garments with images and prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on images on clothing during prayer and distinguish between visible and covered images.

Core Idea
Images on clothing are disliked (makruh), but if covered during prayer, there is no harm.

The presence of images on one's clothing can raise questions about the validity of prayer. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position based on al-Ghunya and al-Khulāṣah. Understanding the distinction between visible and concealed images is key to applying the ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is wearing a garment with images of living beings. According to the Hanafi school, the ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked) for visible images.
This ruling applies whether one is praying or not.
2
Separate the two scenarios
The passage presents two scenarios: (1) images on visible parts of the garment, which are disliked; (2) images on parts covered during prayer (e.g., the hand inside a sleeve, a ring under a sleeve), which are excused.
The key factor is visibility, not mere presence.
3
Apply the principle of coverage
If the image is covered by clothing during prayer, there is no harm because it is not visible. This is derived from the text: 'if it is on his hand and he prays, there is no harm because it is covered by his clothes.'
The same applies to images on a ring if covered.
4
Note the source authority
This ruling is from later Hanafi works (al-Ghunya and al-Khulāṣah), which are considered fatawa mutakhkhirin (later fatwa sources).
It represents the mufta bihi (operative) position.
5
Distinguish from other schools
Other madhahib may have stricter rulings, such as prohibiting any image of a living being on clothing during prayer.
This difference is legitimate (mukhtalaf fih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولُبْسُ ثَوْب ذي صور.
[1] قوله : ولبس ثوب ... الخ ؛ قال في «الغُنية»: تكره التصاوير على الثوب صَلَّى فيه أو لم يصل، أما إذا كانت في يده وهو يصلّي فلا بأس به ؛ لأنه مستور بثيابه، وكذا لو كان على خاتمه. كذا في «الخلاصة».
And wearing a garment with images. [1] His statement: and wearing a garment... etc.; [Author] said in al-Ghunya: 'Images on the garment are disliked, whether one prays in it or not. However, if [the image] is on his hand while he prays, there is no harm because it is covered by his clothes. Similarly if it is on his ring.' As in al-Khulāṣah.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on wearing a garment that has images (pictures of living beings). According to al-Ghunya, such images are makruh (disliked) on the garment, whether one prays in it or not. However, if the image is on the hand (like a tattoo or ring design) and it is covered by the sleeve during prayer, there is no harm. Similarly, an image on a ring is excused if covered. This is from al-Khulāṣah. The general rule is that images that are not visible during prayer are not problematic, but visible images on clothing are disliked.

Key Terms
صور (ṣuwar): images or pictures of living beings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) When it is on the hand and covered by clothes

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, images on clothing are disliked (makruh) during prayer only if visible; covered images cause no issue.

Ruling on Sexual Intercourse, Urination, and Defecation on the Mosque Roof
Ruling on acts on the mosque roof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sexual intercourse, urination, and defecation on the mosque roof and explain the reasoning that the roof shares the same rulings as the mosque.

Core Idea
The mosque roof shares the same sanctity as the mosque interior—impure acts there are makruh.

This passage comes from a commentary on al-Hidayah, explaining why a chapter on prayer includes a ruling about sexual intercourse, urination, and defecation on the mosque roof. The author establishes that the roof is legally part of the mosque, so acts that violate its sanctity are disliked (makruh).

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
The passage lists three acts: sexual intercourse, urination, and defecation on the mosque roof. The ruling is that they are makruh (disliked). The author notes that these are mentioned because they relate to the mosque, even though the chapter is about prayer.
2
Understand the legal status of the mosque roof
The roof is treated as part of the mosque for several rulings: it is valid to follow an imam from the roof in prayer, i'tikaf is not invalidated by going onto the roof, and a person in janabah may not stay on the roof. This establishes that the roof shares the same sanctity.
3
Identify the evidence
The hadith commanding that mosques be cleaned and perfumed implies that acts which bring impurity or disrespect are disliked.
The hadith is cited from Sunan Abi Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوطء والبول والتخلي فوق مسجد.
[2] قوله : والوطء ؛ هذه المسألة وإن لم يكن فيها كراهة الصلاة، لكن بما كانت متعلقة بالمسجد، وهو موضع الصلاة ذكرها هاهنا ؛ أي يكره الوطء أي المجامعة بالنساء. والبول والتخلّي : أي التغوط على سطح المسجد ؛ لأنه في حكم المسجد، حتى يصح الاقتداء منه بمن تحته ، ولا يبطل الاعتكاف بالصعود إليه، ولا يحل للجنب الوقوف عليه، وقد أمر رسول الله أن تنظف المساجد وتطيب) (2) ، أخرجه أبو داود وابن ماجة وغيرهما.
(2) فعن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: «أمر رسول الله ل ببناء المساجد في الدور وأن تنظف وتطيب» في «سنن أبي داود (۱) : (۱۷۸) ، و (سنن الترمذي (۲) : (٤۸۹)، و(سنن ابن ماجة» (۱ : ٢٥۱)، وغيرها.
And sexual intercourse, urination, and defecation above a mosque. [2] His statement: and sexual intercourse; this issue, although there is no dislike in prayer, but because it is related to the mosque, which is the place of prayer, he mentioned it here; meaning it is disliked: sexual intercourse (i.e., with women), urination, and defecation (i.e., excreting) on the roof of the mosque; because it is subject to the same ruling as the mosque, to the point that it is valid to follow (in prayer) someone who is below by being on the roof, and iʿtikāf is not invalidated by going up to it, and it is not permissible for a person in janābah to stand on it, and the Messenger of Allah ordered that mosques be cleaned and perfumed (2), reported by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah and others. (2) From ʿĀʾishah (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered that mosques be built in dwellings and that they be cleaned and perfumed' in Sunan Abi Dawud (1:178), Sunan al-Tirmidhi (2:489), Sunan Ibn Majah (1:251), etc.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage addresses acts that are makruh (disliked) on the mosque roof. Even though the chapter is about prayer, these acts are mentioned because they relate to the mosque, which is the place of prayer. The ruling: sexual intercourse, urination, and defecation on the mosque roof are all makruh. This is because the roof is treated like the mosque itself: it is valid for a person on the roof to follow an imam below (in congregational prayer), iʿtikāf is not invalidated by going onto the roof, and a person in a state of ritual impurity (janābah) may not stay on the roof. The hadith cited commands cleaning and perfuming mosques.

Key Terms
الوطء (al-waṭʾ): sexual intercourse
التخلي (al-takhallī): defecation

Ruling on Locking the Mosque Door
Ruling on locking the mosque door

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on locking the mosque door and identify the condition that makes it permissible.

Core Idea
Locking the mosque door is generally makruh but allowed when needed for protection.

The mosque is a place of worship meant to be open for prayer and remembrance of Allah. However, there are times when locking its door becomes necessary for protection. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on this act, balancing the general principle against exceptional circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The text states that locking the mosque door is disliked (makruh). Understand that this is the default ruling.
The ruling is from a later Hanafi work, al-Bināyah.
2
Understand the proof
The author cites Quran 2:114, comparing locking to preventing prayer. Consider how the analogy is drawn.
The dalalah is zanni because it is an analogy.
3
Note the exception
If there is fear for the mosque's belongings and it is not prayer time, locking is allowed. This is the condition that lifts the dislike.
This exception is based on necessity (istihsan).
4
Classify the hukm
Overall, the act is makruh tanzihi (disliked) without excuse, and mubah (permissible) with a valid excuse.
Some later scholars even allow it without excuse, but the mufta bihi is the nuanced position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغلق بابه.
[3] قوله : وغلق ؛ بفتح الغين المعجمة ؛ أي يكره غلق باب المسجد ؛ لأنه يشبه المنع من الصلاة ، وقد قال الله : وَمَنْ أَظْلَمُ مِمَّن مَنَعَ مَسَاجِدَ اللَّهِ أَن يُذْكَرَ فِيهَا اسْمُهُ (3) ، وقيل : لا بأس إذا خيف على متاع المسجد ، وكان في غير أوان الصلاة. كذا في «البناية».
(3) البقرة : من الآية ١١٤ .
And locking its door. [3] His statement: and locking (ghalaq) with fatḥa on the ghayn; i.e., it is disliked to lock the door of the mosque because it resembles preventing prayer, and Allah said: 'And who is more unjust than one who prevents [people] from the mosques of Allah, [where] His name is mentioned?' (3) And it is said: there is no harm if one fears for the mosque's belongings and it is not during prayer time. As in al-Bināyah. (3) Surah al-Baqarah, verse 114.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on locking the mosque door. It is makruh (disliked) because locking the door resembles preventing people from entering the mosque for prayer, which is a great injustice (as per Quran 2:114). However, there is an exception: if there is a fear of theft or damage to the mosque's belongings, and it is not prayer time, then it is permissible to lock the door. This is from al-Bināyah.

Key Terms

Key Takeaway

Ruling on Counting Dhikr in Prayer
Explaining the ruling on counting dhikr with hand during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each method of counting dhikr during salah and distinguish between actions that are makruh tanzih and those that invalidate prayer.

Core Idea
Counting dhikr with the hand is mildly disliked; counting with the tongue invalidates prayer.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on counting dhikr during salah. The source distinguishes between permissible, disliked, and invalidating methods. Understanding these distinctions helps maintain the integrity and khushu' of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the ruling concerns the act of counting dhikr (e.g., tasbih, tahmid) during prayer.
2
Identify the methods
The text discusses three ways: counting with the hand (fingers or thread), pressing with fingertips, and counting with the tongue.
3
Determine the ruling for each
For hand: makruh tanzih; for fingertips: not disliked by consensus; for tongue: invalidates prayer by consensus.
4
Note the level of dislike and exceptions
The dislike is tanzihi, and there is a view that hand counting is not disliked in nafl prayers.
5
Understand the basis
The ruling is because it is not from the actions of prayer and contradicts khushu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر في «البحر» و «الحلبة» و«البناية» وغيرها : أن محل الخلاف إنما هو العد باليد، سواء كان بأصبعه أو بخيط يمسكه، أما الغمز برؤوس الأصابع والحفظ بالقلب فلا يكره اتفاقا، والعد باللسان مفسد اتفاقا. وقيد بالآي والتسبيح ; لأن عد غيرهما مكروه اتفاقا، والكراهة هاهنا تنزيهية ; لكونه ليس من أعمال الصلاة ومنافيا للخشوع، وفي الإطلاق إشارة إلى الكراهة في التطوع والمكتوبة كليهما، وقيل : لا يكره في النوافل، وهذا كله في الصلاة، وأما عدا الأذكار خارجها فلا يكره، سواء كان باليد أو بالسبحة، وقد فصلت الكلام على هذه المسائل في رسالتي نزهة الفكر في سبحة الذكر.
It is mentioned in 'Al-Bahr', 'Al-Halba', 'Al-Binaya', and others: that the point of disagreement is only regarding counting with the hand, whether with one's finger or with a thread he holds. As for pressing with the fingertips and memorizing with the heart, it is not disliked by agreement. And counting with the tongue invalidates [the prayer] by agreement. And it is restricted to verses and tasbih; because counting other than them is disliked by agreement. And the dislike here is tanzihi (mildly disliked) because it is not from the actions of prayer and is contrary to khushu' (humility). And the absolute expression indicates dislike in both nafl and obligatory prayers. And it is said: it is not disliked in nafl prayers. And all of this is in prayer. As for other remembrances outside of prayer, it is not disliked, whether with the hand or with the prayer beads. And I have detailed the discussion on these issues in my treatise 'Nuzhat al-Fikr fi Subhat al-Dhikr'.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on counting dhikr (remembrance) during prayer. The author clarifies that the difference of opinion is specifically about counting with the hand, whether with the finger or with a thread. Pressing with fingertips or memorizing with the heart is not disliked by consensus. However, counting with the tongue invalidates the prayer by consensus. The ruling is restricted to counting verses (آي) and tasbih (تسبيح); counting other things is disliked by agreement. The dislike is tanzihi (mildly makruh) because it is not part of the actions of prayer and it reduces khushu'. The author notes that some say there is no dislike in supererogatory prayers. Outside of prayer, there is no dislike in counting dhikr by any means. The Hanafi school generally regards counting with the hand as makruh tanzih, while counting with the tongue is nullifying (mufsid).

Key Terms
العد باليد (al-addu bil-yad): Using the hand to count dhikr, e.g., by moving fingers or holding a thread.
الغمز برؤوس الأصابع (al-ghamzu bi ru'us al-asabi'): Pressing the tips of fingers to count, not disliked by consensus.
العد باللسان (al-addu bil-lisan): Counting dhikr by moving the tongue, which invalidates prayer by consensus.
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyyah): A level of dislike that is not prohibited but discouraged, typically not sinful.
مفسد (mufsid): Something that invalidates the act of worship, requiring repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for counting dhikr with the hand during prayer according to the text?
A) It invalidates the prayer.
B) It is makruh tanzih.
C) It is permissible and recommended.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Counting dhikr with the hand is mildly disliked (makruh tanzih); counting with the tongue invalidates the prayer by consensus.

Core Idea
Images on clothing are disliked, but if covered during prayer, there is no issue.

This lesson addresses a common concern: does having an image on one's clothing affect the validity of salah? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling, distinguishing between visible images and those that are concealed. We will examine the source text from Al-Ghunya and Al-Khulasa to understand the precise ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wearing a garment with images. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked) based on the text from Al-Ghunya.
Dislike does not invalidate prayer.
2
Distinguish between scenarios
The text distinguishes between the image being on the garment (disliked whether in prayer or not) and on a part that is covered during prayer (no problem).
The key factor is visibility.
3

Actions Disliked on the Mosque Roof and Closing Its Door
Rulings with proof on mosque roof actions and closing its door.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse, urination, defecation on the mosque roof and closing its door, and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
The mosque roof shares the mosque's sanctity; violating it or blocking access is disliked.

This lesson addresses four actions related to the mosque: intercourse, urination, defecation on its roof, and closing its door. While these actions do not directly affect prayer, they are mentioned here because they concern the mosque, the place of prayer. You will learn the Hanafi rulings and the proofs from the Quran and Sunnah that support them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and their common link
List the four actions mentioned: al-wat' (intercourse), al-bawl (urination), al-takhalli (defecation) on the mosque roof, and ghalaq al-bab (closing the door). Note that they all relate to the mosque's sanctity.
The roof is legally equivalent to the mosque itself.
2
Understand the legal status of the mosque roof
The text clarifies that the roof (sath) of the mosque is in the same ruling as the mosque: it is valid to follow an imam from the roof, i'tikaf is not invalidated by ascending it, and a junub cannot stand on it. This establishes the roof's sanctity.
This shared ruling is why the actions are disliked.
3
Examine the evidence for each ruling
For intercourse, urination, and defecation, the evidence is the hadith commanding cleanliness of mosques. For closing the door, the evidence is the Quranic verse (2:114) warning against preventing access to mosques.
The hadith is reported by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah.
4
Note the exception for closing the door
The text mentions an exception from Al-Binaya: if there is fear for the mosque's belongings and it is not a prayer time, closing the door is not blameworthy.
This exception is based on necessity (istihsan).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوطء والبول والتخلي فوق مسجد، وغلق بابه. قوله : والوطء ; هذه المسألة وإن لم يكن فيها كراهة الصلاة، لكن بما كانت متعلقة بالمسجد، وهو موضع الصلاة ذكرها هاهنا ; أي يكره الوطء أي المجامعة بالنساء. والبول والتخلّي : أي التغوط على سطح المسجد ; لأنه في حكم المسجد، حتى يصح الاقتداء منه بمن تحته ، ولا يبطل الاعتكاف بالصعود إليه، ولا يحل للجنب الوقوف عليه، وقد أمر رسول الله أن تنظف المساجد وتطيب) ، أخرجه أبو داود وابن ماجة وغيرهما. قوله : وغلق ; بفتح الغين المعجمة ; أي يكره غلق باب المسجد ; لأنه يشبه المنع من الصلاة ، وقد قال الله : وَمَنْ أَظْلَمُ مِمَّن مَنَعَ مَسَاجِدَ اللَّهِ أَن يُذْكَرَ فِيهَا اسْمُهُ (۳) ، وقيل : لا بأس إذا خيف على متاع المسجد ، وكان في غير أوان الصلاة. كذا في «البناية».
And intercourse, urination, and defecation on a mosque, and closing its door. He said: 'And intercourse' - this issue, even though it does not involve dislike in prayer, but because it relates to the mosque, which is the place of prayer, it is mentioned here. So it is disliked to have intercourse, i.e., sexual relations with women. And urination and defecation: i.e., excreting on the roof of the mosque, because it is in the ruling of the mosque. So much so that it is valid to follow (in prayer) from one on the roof to the one below, and itikaf is not invalidated by ascending to it, and it is not permissible for a junub to stand on it. And the Messenger of Allah ordered that mosques be cleaned and perfumed, reported by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, and others. He said: 'And closing' with fatha on the ghain mu'jama: i.e., it is disliked to close the door of the mosque, because it resembles preventing prayer. And Allah said: 'And who is more unjust than one who prevents the mosques of Allah from mentioning His name therein' (2:114). And it is said: there is no harm if one fears for the mosque's belongings and it is not the time of prayer. Thus in Al-Binaya.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage discusses four actions related to the mosque that are disliked. First, having sexual intercourse (الوطء) on the mosque roof is disliked because the roof shares the same rulings as the mosque itself. Second, urination (البول) and defecation (التخلي) on the roof are also disliked, as the roof has the same legal status as the mosque. The proof for cleaning the mosque is the hadith commanding cleanliness and perfuming. Third, closing the door of the mosque is disliked because it can be seen as preventing people from entering to pray. The Quranic verse (2:114) is cited as evidence. However, if there is fear for the mosque's belongings and it is not a prayer time, it is permissible. These rulings are from the Hanafi school, as mentioned in Al-Binaya.

Key Terms
الوطء (al-wat'): Sexual intercourse, specifically on the mosque roof, which is disliked.
البول (al-bawl): Urination, on the mosque roof, disliked.
التخلي (al-takhalli): Defecation, on the mosque roof, disliked.
سطح المسجد (sath al-masjid): The roof of the mosque, which shares the rulings of the mosque.
غلق باب المسجد (ghalaq bab al-masjid): Closing the door of the mosque, which is disliked unless necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in the passage, when is it not blameworthy to close the mosque door?
A) When the imam wants to pray alone.
B) When there is fear for the mosque's belongings and it is not a prayer time.
C) When it is very cold outside.
D) When the mosque is under renovation.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse, urination, and defecation on the mosque roof are disliked (makruh tanzih) because the roof shares the mosque's rulings, and closing the door is also disliked except when necessary to protect property outside prayer times.

Ruling on Decorating the Mosque with Plaster, Teak, and Gold Water
Explaining the difference of opinion on beautifying the mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on decorating the mosque and distinguish between the three scholarly opinions based on their evidence.

Core Idea
Mosque decoration is permissible in itself, but disliked if it leads to neglect of prayer.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya addresses the ruling on beautifying mosques. After discussing disliked actions in prayer, the author turns to what is not disliked. There is a difference of opinion among scholars, and the Hanafi school adopts a nuanced view that balances reverence and practicality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is decorating the mosque (naqsh al-masjid) with materials like plaster, teak, and gold water. The matn states it is not disliked (la yukrah).
2
Recognize the three scholarly positions
The commentary lists three opinions: qurbah (commendable), makruh (disliked), and ja'iz (permissible). Note the evidence for each.
3
Analyze the evidence for each position
Qurbah is based on glorifying the mosque. Makruh is supported by a hadith: 'From the signs of the Hour is the adornment of mosques.' Ja'iz interprets that hadith as conditional on neglect.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its meaning is interpreted.
4
Determine the Hanafi mufta bihi
The chosen view (mukhtar) of the author of Al-Hidayah and others is that it is ja'iz (permissible) but better to avoid. The karaha (dislike) applies only when accompanied by extravagance or neglect of prayer.
This resolution balances the hadith and the principle of respect for mosques.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Consider modern examples: installing ornamental lights, carpets, or calligraphy. The key is that decoration should not distract from worship or lead to pride.
The ruling is general; specific cases may require further ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا نقشه بالجص والسّاج وماء الذهب. قوله : لا نقشه ; لَمَّا فَرَغَ عن ذكر ما يكره في الصلاة وما يتعلق بها، شرع في ذكر ما لا يكره : أي لا يكره نقش المسجد وتزيينه بالجص، وهو بفتح الجيم، وتشديد الصاد المهملة، معرب كج ، وكذا بماء الذهب وبالساج ونحوه، وهو نوع من الخشب يقال له : ساكون أفضل أنواعه وأحكمه، وقد وقع فيه الخلاف : فقيل : إنه قربة لما فيه من تعظيم المسجد. وقيل : مكروه؛ لحديث: من أشراط الساعة أن تزين المساجد»(4). وقيل : جائز غير مكروه، نعم الأفضل غيره، وهو مختار صاحب «الهداية» وغيرها، ومحمل الكراهة التكلف، قالوا : النقوش ونحوه، خصوصا في المحراب، أو التزين مع ترك الصلاة أو عدم إعطائه حقه من اللغط فيه، والجلوس لحديث الدنيا، ورفع الأصوات بدليل آخر الحديث، وهو قوله : «وقلوبهم خاوية من الإيمان». كذا في «فتح القدير»).
It is not disliked to adorn it with plaster, teak, and gold water. He said: 'It is not disliked to adorn it' - when he finished mentioning what is disliked in prayer and related matters, he began to mention what is not disliked: i.e., it is not disliked to engrave the mosque and decorate it with plaster, with fatha on the jim and shadda on the sad, a Persian word, and also with gold water and teak and the like, which is a type of wood called sakun, the best and most solid type. And there is a difference of opinion regarding it: some said it is a means of drawing near because it glorifies the mosque. Some said it is disliked due to the hadith: 'From the signs of the Hour is the adornment of mosques.' Some said it is permissible and not disliked, and indeed it is better to avoid it, and this is the choice of the author of Al-Hidayah and others. And the interpretation of the dislike is exaggeration. They said: inscriptions and the like, especially in the mihrab, or adornment while neglecting prayer or not giving it its due from idle talk, sitting for worldly talk, and raising voices, as indicated by the rest of the hadith: 'And their hearts are empty of faith.' Thus in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on decorating mosques. After listing disliked actions in prayer, the author now lists what is not disliked. The matn states that it is not disliked to decorate the mosque with plaster, teak, and gold water. The commentator explains that there are three opinions: 1) It is a commendable act (qurbah) because it glorifies the mosque. 2) It is disliked (makruh) based on the hadith that mosque adornment is a sign of the Hour. 3) It is permissible (ja'iz) and not disliked, but it is better to avoid it. This last opinion is the chosen view of the author of Al-Hidayah and others. The textual evidence for the permissibility is that the dislike applies only when there is extravagance or neglect of prayer. The hadith regarding the signs of the Hour is interpreted as applying when the adornment is accompanied by empty hearts. Therefore, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is not disliked in principle, but it may become disliked if it leads to negligence in worship.

Key Terms
نقش (naqsh): Engraving or decoration, especially in the context of mosque adornment.
جص (jass): Plaster, used for building and decoration.
ساج (saj): Teak wood, used for construction and decoration.
ماء الذهب (ma' al-dhahab): Gold water or gilding, used for decoration.

A) It is a recommended act (qurbah).

D) It is forbidden (haram).

Key Takeaway
Mosque decoration is permissible in itself, but it becomes disliked if it leads to distraction from worship or involves extravagance.

Ruling on the Imam's Prostration in the Mihrab
Explaining that it is not disliked for the imam to prostrate while standing in the mihrab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the imam's prostration in the mihrab is not disliked (makruh) according to the Hanafi school, citing the absence of the effective cause (illah).

Core Idea
No dislike if the cause of dislike is absent.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies a common concern about the imam's posture during prayer. Some wondered whether prostrating inside the mihrab (prayer niche) might be disliked because it resembles practices of other religions or could confuse the congregation. The Hanafi ruling addresses this by focusing on the effective cause (illah) — if the reason for dislike does not exist, the action reverts to its original permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act under discussion is the imam prostrating while standing inside the mihrab during prayer. The default ruling for actions in prayer is permissibility unless there is a specific prohibition.
Note: The act is part of the prayer itself, not an extra action.
2
Understand the potential cause for dislike
The passage mentions two possible causes: resembling the People of the Book (tashabbuh bi ahl al-kitab) and causing confusion for the followers (khawf ishtibah halihi 'ala al-mu'tamin). Both would make the action makruh if present.
Resemblance to non-Muslims in worship can be makruh tahrimi.
3
Determine whether the cause is present
In this scenario, the imam is prostrating inside the mihrab. The commentator argues that neither cause exists: standing in the mihrab while prostrating does not inherently resemble the practices of other religions, nor does it confuse the followers because they can see the imam's posture clearly.
The mihrab is a standard architectural feature of mosques, not exclusively associated with other faiths.
4
Derive the final ruling
Since the effective cause (illah) for dislike is absent, the original permissibility remains. Therefore, the act is not disliked (la yukrah). It is considered mubah (permissible) or even better, but not obligatory or recommended beyond the normal prayer.
The ruling is mufta bihi and agreed upon within the Hanafi school.

Source Text

And his standing in it prostrating in his arch. He said: 'And his standing' - i.e., it is not disliked for the imam to stand in the mosque while he is prostrating in his mihrab, because the cause of dislike is absent in it, namely resembling the People of the Book, or the fear of confusion of his state for the followers present due to his standing in the mihrab.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage addresses the concern about the imam prostrating while standing in the mihrab (prayer niche). The matn clarifies that it is not disliked. The commentator explains that the reason for any potential dislike was to avoid resembling the People of the Book or to prevent confusion for the followers. Since those reasons are not present, the action is not disliked. In the Hanafi school, the imam may pray in the mihrab without any dislike.

Key Terms

ساجداً (sajidan): Prostrating, the posture of prostration.
محراب (mihrab): Prayer niche in the mosque showing direction of qibla.
طاق (taq): Arch, niche; synonymous with mihrab in this context.
علة الكراهة (illat al-karahah): The effective cause that would make the action disliked.

Ruling on Decorating Mosques
Explains ruling on mosque decoration with scholarly disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mosque decoration and distinguish the three scholarly positions based on their proofs.

Core Idea
Mosque decoration is permissible but better avoided; dislike only when it distracts.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah addresses a classical debate: is it permissible to decorate mosques with materials like gypsum, teak, or gold water? The author presents three views before settling on the Hanafi preferred position. Understanding this ruling requires weighing textual evidence against the goal of venerating the mosque.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses engraving or adorning the mosque (naqsh al-masjid) with gypsum, teak, and gold water. The initial statement is 'لا نقشه' (do not engrave it), which the commentator explains means it is not disliked (la yukrah).
The commentator clarifies the matn's apparent prohibition is actually a negation of dislike.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'Among the signs of the Hour is that mosques will be adorned' is cited as evidence by those who dislike decoration. The commentator notes he did not find this exact wording but similar traditions exist.
The hadith is of zanni thubut, and its dalala is also zanni, allowing for interpretation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Those who dislike decoration argue that adornment is a sign of the Hour, implying it is blameworthy. The Hanafi response reinterprets the hadith: the dislike applies only when decoration involves extravagance (takalluf) or leads to neglect of prayer.
The rest of the hadith ('hearts empty of faith') supports the condition of spiritual emptiness.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Three positions exist: (1) qurbah (good deed) because it glorifies the mosque, (2) makruh based on the hadith, (3) ja'iz (permissible) but better to avoid—this is the mukhtar of al-Hidayah.
The ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school and also across schools.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is permissibility, with dislike restricted to cases of extravagance or distraction from worship. This is endorsed by the commentator and supported by Fath al-Qadir.
The tarjih balances the hadith's warning with the goal of venerating the mosque.

Source Text

[ ١ ] قوله : لا نقشه ؛ لَمَّا فَرَغَ عن ذكر ما يكره في الصلاة وما يتعلق بها، شرع في ذكر ما لا يكره : أي لا يكره نقش المسجد وتزيينه بالجص، وهو بفتح الجيم، وتشديد الصاد المهملة، معرب كج ، وكذا بماء الذهب وبالساج ونحوه، وهو نوع من الخشب يقال له : ساكون أفضل أنواعه وأحكمه، وقد وقع فيه الخلاف :

فقيل : إنه قربة لما فيه من تعظيم المسجد.
وقيل : مكروه؛ لحديث: من أشراط الساعة أن تزين المساجد»(4).
وقيل : جائز غير مكروه، نعم الأفضل غيره، وهو مختار صاحب «الهداية» وغيرها، ومحمل الكراهة التكلف، قالوا : النقوش ونحوه، خصوصا في المحراب، أو التزين مع ترك الصلاة أو عدم إعطائه حقه من اللغط فيه، والجلوس لحديث الدنيا، ورفع الأصوات بدليل آخر الحديث، وهو قوله : «وقلوبهم خاوية من الإيمان». كذا في «فتح القدير»)

(1) الجص : بفتح الجيم وكسرها : ما يبنى به وهو معرب. ينظر: «مختار»(ص١٠٤). (2) الساج : خشب يجلب من الهند والسَّاج شجر يعظم جداً، ويذهب طولاً وعرضاً، وله ورق يتغطى الرجل بشجرة منه، وله رائحة طيبة تشابه ورق الجوز مع رقة ونعمة. ينظر: «اللسان)» (٣ : ٢١٤١). He (the author) said: 'Do not engrave it with gypsum, teak, and gold water.' [1] His statement: 'Do not engrave it' – when he finished mentioning what is disliked in prayer and what pertains to it, he began to mention what is not disliked: meaning, it is not disliked to engrave (decorate) the mosque and adorn it with gypsum (which is with a fatha on the jim and tashdid on the sad, being a Persianized word 'gach'), and similarly with gold water and with teak and the like. Teak is a type of wood, the best and strongest kind. There is disagreement about it: Some said it is a good deed because it glorifies the mosque. Some said it is disliked due to the hadith: 'Among the signs of the Hour is that mosques will be adorned.' Some said it is permissible without dislike, but something else is better; this is the chosen view of the author of al-Hidayah and others. The interpretation of dislike is when it involves extravagance. They said: Engravings and the like, especially in the mihrab, or adornment while abandoning prayer or not giving the mosque its due of noise, sitting for worldly talk, and raising voices, as indicated by the rest of the hadith: 'While their hearts are empty of faith.' (2) Teak: wood brought from India, a huge tree, its leaf covers a man, smells like walnut leaves. (4) I did not find this wording, but Abd al-Razzaq recorded in his Musannaf close traditions about adorning mosques, and similarly Abu Amr in al-Sunan al-Waridah. (5) Fath al-Qadir.

Commentary
This is a ruling_with_proof passage from the sharh (commentary) of al-Wiqayah, explaining the matn's statement 'لا نقشه' (do not engrave it). The commentator clarifies that the phrase refers to mosque decoration with materials like gypsum, teak, and gold water. He presents the scholarly disagreement: some consider it a good deed, others dislike it based on a hadith about signs of the Hour, and the preferred view (mukhtar of al-Hidayah) is that it is permissible but better to avoid. The dislike is interpreted as applying only when there is extravagance or when adornment leads to neglecting the mosque's purpose. The commentary cites Fath al-Qadir to support this interpretation.

الساج (al-saj): Teak wood, considered the best wood type.
ماء الذهب (ma' al-dhahab): Gold water, used for gilding.
النقش (al-naqsh): Engraving or decorative carving.
التكلف (al-takalluf): Extravagance or unnecessary elaboration in decoration.

Ruling on Imam's Standing and Prostrating in the Mihrab
States that imam's standing and prostrating in the mihrab is not disliked.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's standing and prostrating in the mihrab and explain why the cause of dislike is absent.

Core Idea
The imam's standing and prostrating in the mihrab is not disliked because the cause of dislike—imitating People of the Book or confusing followers—does not apply.

This passage explains a concise statement from the matn regarding the imam's position in the mihrab. The commentator clarifies that the act is not disliked, using talil (rational reasoning) to identify the effective cause (illah) and confirm its absence. Understanding this method helps us see how Hanafi scholars derive rulings from underlying principles rather than relying solely on explicit texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The matn mentions 'qiyamuhu fihi sajidan fi taqih' (his standing in it, prostrating in his niche). The commentator states it is not disliked (la yukrah) for the imam to stand and prostrate in the mihrab.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) – no dislike.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The proof is the absence of the illat al-karaha (cause of dislike). The commentator explicitly mentions two possible causes: tashabbuh bi ahl al-kitab (imitating People of the Book) or khawf ishtibah halih (fear of confusing the followers).
This is a talil argument—reasoning from cause.
3
Understand the Wajh al-Dalalah
The ruling is based on the absence of the cause: since neither imitation nor confusion occurs when the imam simply stands and prostrates in the mihrab, the ruling of dislike is lifted. The wajh is that permissibility is the default unless a cause for prohibition or dislike is present.
The Hanafi principle: al-asl fi al-ashya' al-ibaha.
4
Note Potential Ikhtilaf
Some might consider it disliked based on general principles of avoiding innovations. However, the commentator resolves this by specifying the exact cause and its absence, thus confirming the preferred view of no dislike.
The Hanafi position relies on precise illah identification.

The reason for the absence of dislike is that the usual cause of dislike—either imitating People of the Book or creating confusion for the followers about the imam's state—does not apply here. The ruling is based on rational reasoning (talil), identifying the effective cause and its absence.

Ruling on Praying Behind a Sitting Person Who Is Talking
Explains that praying behind a sitting talking person is not disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying behind a sitting talking person and distinguish when it is disliked versus permitted.

Core Idea
Praying behind a talking person is not disliked; only facing the face is disliked.

The passage clarifies a common misconception: it is not necessarily disliked to pray facing the back of someone who is sitting and talking. The Hanafi school provides clear evidence from the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) and Ibn 'Umar, and addresses a weak hadith that might suggest otherwise. Understanding this ruling helps avoid unnecessary restrictions in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Read the first sentence: 'وصلاته إلى ظهر قاعد يتحدث . . . لا تكره'. The act is praying towards the back of a sitting person who is talking. The ruling is that it is not disliked (mubah).
The word 'لا تكره' explicitly negates karaha.
2
Analyze the incidental condition
The text states that the restriction to 'sitting' (قاعد) is incidental (اتفاقي); the ruling is the same if the person is standing or lying down. Understand that the key is facing the back, not the posture.
This shows the Hanafi focus on effective cause rather than literal wording.
3
Examine the implication of 'talking'
The text says that if the person is not talking, it is even less disliked (بالطريق الأولى). So talking does not make it disliked; the ruling is permissive in both cases.
This is an a fortiori argument (qiyas awlawi).
4
Distinguish facing back vs. face
The specification of 'back' (ظهر) indicates that facing the face is disliked. Understand that the prohibition is only when one faces the face directly, as that may resemble distraction.
The evidence from the Prophet's prayer with 'A'isha shows that having someone in front is not inherently a problem.
5
Evaluate the conflicting weak hadith
The hadith 'لا تصلوا خلف النائم والمتحدث' is weak; even if authentic, the Hanafis interpret it as applying only when there is fear of distraction (رفع أصواتهم). This demonstrates the principle that weak evidence is set aside by stronger practice.
This step shows the Hanafi methodology of tarjih (preference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلاته إلى ظهر قاعد يتحدث

[1]قوله : وصلاته ؛ أي لا تكره صلاة المصلّي إلى ظهر رجل قاعد متحدّث : أي متكلم مع آخر ، وقيد القعود اتفاقي ، فإنّ الحكم لا يختلف فيما إذا كان قائماً أو مضطجعاً، وفهم من قيد التحدث أنه لو لم يكن متحدثاً لم يكره بالطريق الأولى. وفي تقييد الظهر إشارة إلى أنه يكره مواجها لوجهه ، وقد صح أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يُصلّي وعائشة رضي الله عنهم معترضة بين يديه كاعتراض الجنازة)، رواه الشيخان. وأخرج ابن أبي شيبة أن ابن عمر : كان إذا لم يجد سبيلاً إلى سارية من سواري المسجد، قال لنافع : ولّني ظهرك). وأما ما في سنن أبي داود وابن ماجه مرفوعاً: «لا تصلوا خلف النائم والمتحدث» (۳) ، فسنده ضعيف وعلى تقدير صحته فهو محمول على ما إذا خافَ الشغل والغلط برفع أصواتهم ونحوه. كذا في «العناية»، و«شرح المنية».
And his prayer towards the back of a sitting person who is talking. [1] His statement: 'and his prayer' – i.e., it is not disliked for the person praying to pray towards the back of a sitting person who is speaking (i.e., talking with another). The restriction to 'sitting' is incidental; the ruling does not differ whether he is standing or lying down. It is understood from the restriction 'talking' that if he is not talking, it is not disliked by even greater reason. The specification of 'back' indicates that facing his face is disliked. It is authentically reported that the Messenger of Allah (صلى الله عليه وسلم) used to pray while 'A'isha (رضي الله عنها) lay between him and the qibla like a bier, as narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. Ibn Abi Shayba recorded that Ibn 'Umar, when he could not find a way to one of the mosque pillars, would say to Nafi': 'Turn your back to me.' As for what is in Sunan Abi Dawud and Ibn Majah as a marfu' hadith: 'Do not pray behind a sleeping or talking person,' its chain is weak, and even if authentic, it is interpreted as applying when one fears distraction and error due to their raising voices, etc. As in al-'Inaya and Sharh al-Munya.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This is a ruling_with_proof passage. The commentator explains that it is not disliked to pray facing the back of a person who is sitting and talking. The condition of 'sitting' is not essential; the same applies if the person is standing or lying. Not talking makes it even less disliked. Facing the face is disliked, as established by the practice of the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) and Ibn 'Umar. The hadith prohibiting prayer behind sleeping or talking persons is weak; even if accepted, it applies only when there is a risk of distraction. The Hanafi position is based on authentic practice and preference for ease.

Key Terms
قاعد (qa'id): A sitting person; the ruling applies even if standing or lying.
متحدث (mutahaddith): A person talking (speaking) with another.
اتفاقي (ittifaqi): Incidental; not essential to the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is the ruling on praying towards the back of a person who is sitting and talking?
A) It is disliked (makruh).
B) It is invalid (batil).
C) It is not disliked (لا يكره).
D) It is a confirmed sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Praying facing the back of a sitting talking person is not disliked; the Hanafi position is based on authentic practice and sets aside a weak contrary hadith.

Praying on a Mat with Images: The Hanafi Condition
Explains the permissibility of praying on a mat with images if not prostrating on them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying on a mat with images and explain the condition of avoiding prostration on images, using the hadith of 'A'isha as proof.

Core Idea
Praying on a mat with images is permissible if you do not prostrate on the images.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah addresses a common concern: is it permissible to pray on a mat that has pictures of animals? The Hanafi position clarifies that as long as the images are not in the place of prostration, the prayer is valid. The ruling is supported by a well-known hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Ruling
Identify the legal classification (hukm) of praying on a mat with images. The passage says it is 'not disliked' (la tukrah), meaning it is permissible (mubah).
The ruling is permissive, not mandatory.
2
Identify the Condition
Find the explicit condition mentioned: the worshipper must not prostrate on the images. The images should be in the area of standing or sitting, not where the forehead touches.
The Arabic phrase is 'بشرط أن لا يسجد عليها'.
3
Locate the Dalil (Evidence)
The commentator cites the hadith of 'A'isha from Sahih al-Bukhari. The Prophet tore a curtain with figures, but later sat on pillows made from it.
This shows that using items with images for sitting (and by analogy, for prayer) is permissible if not prostrating directly on them.
4
Understand the Wajh al-Dalalah (Proof Indication)
The Prophet's action of tearing the curtain indicates disapproval of images as objects of display, but his sitting on the pillows shows that the prohibition is not absolute. The difference lies in the context: prostration involves direct contact with the image.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle of distinguishing between different contexts of use.
5
Apply to a Scenario
Consider a mat with a small animal image in the center. If you pray on it, ensure the image is not under your forehead during sujood. If it's elsewhere, prayer is valid.
This is the practical implication for daily worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى بساط ذي صور لا يسجد عليها

[٢]قوله : وعلى بساط ؛ أي لا تكره الصلاة على بساط مصور بصورة الحيوان، بشرط أن لا يسجد عليها بأن تكون في موضع قيامه وجلوسه، فإنّ بسط البساط ذي الصور والاستناد على الوسادة التي فيها الصور جائز ) ، ثبت ذلك عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في حديث عائشة: أنها اتخذت على سهوة لها ستراً فيه تماثيل، فهتكه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، قالت: فاتخذت منه نمرقتين فكانتا في البيت يجلس عليهما (في صحيح البخاري).
And on a mat with images, he does not prostrate on them. [2] His statement: 'and on a mat' – i.e., it is not disliked to pray on a mat that is decorated with images of animals, on the condition that one does not prostrate on them (i.e., the images are in the place of his standing and sitting). For spreading a mat with images and leaning on a cushion that has images is permissible. This is established from the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) in the hadith of 'A'isha: That she had a curtain with figures on a shelf of her house; the Prophet tore it; she said: 'I made from it two pillows, and they were in the house, and he would sit on them.' (Reported in Sahih al-Bukhari).
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This is a ruling_with_proof passage. The matn states that it is not disliked to pray on a mat that has images, provided the worshipper does not prostrate on the images themselves. The commentator explains that the images should be in the area where one stands or sits, not where the forehead touches during prostration. This is supported by the hadith of 'A'isha (رضي الله عنها) where the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) disapproved of a curtain with images but later used pillows made from it for sitting. Hence, using such items when not prostrating on the images is permissible by analogy.

Key Terms
بساط (bisat): A mat or carpet spread on the floor.
صور (suwar): Images, especially of animate beings (animals).
نمرقة (numruqah): A cushion or pillow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is it permissible to pray on a mat with images of animals according to this passage?
A) The images must be small.
B) The images must be covered.
C) The worshipper must not prostrate on the images.
D) The mat must be made of plain material.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits prayer on a mat with images provided the worshipper does not prostrate on the images, as evidenced by the Prophet's actions with the curtain and pillows.

Praying Towards a Talking Person: Permissibility
Ruling with proof: permissibility of praying towards a talking person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying towards a seated talking person and identify the key evidence from the Sunnah that supports it.

Core Idea
Praying towards a talking person's back is permissible unless distraction is feared; the contrary hadith is weak.

In this passage, the commentator of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah expands on a succinct matn: one may pray towards the back of a seated person who is talking. The ruling is not disliked—it is mubah. But why would anyone think it could be disliked? Possibly because of a hadith prohibiting prayer behind a sleeping or talking person. This lesson explores how the Hanafi school addresses that hadith and establishes the default permissibility through stronger evidence from the Prophet's own practice and the practice of the Companion Ibn 'Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
The act is praying towards the back of a person who is seated and talking. The ruling: 'la tukrah'—it is not disliked, hence permissible (mubah).
The restriction 'seated' is incidental; same ruling for standing or lying down.
2
Locate the Supporting Evidence
The commentator cites a Sahih hadith: the Prophet ﷺ prayed while 'A'ishah lay in front of him like a bier. Also, Ibn 'Umar instructed Nafi' to turn his back so he could pray towards him.
These show that praying towards a person—even awake—is permissible.
3
Analyse the Wajh al-Dalalah
The Prophet's action is an explicit precedent (fi'l) indicating permissibility. Ibn 'Umar's instruction is a practice of a Companion, used as supporting evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
The wajh is that the Prophet did not change his prayer despite her presence.
4
Note the Contradictory Narration
A marfu' hadith in Sunan Abi Dawud and Ibn Majah states: 'Do not pray behind a sleeping or talking person.' This could suggest prohibition.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Resolution
The Hanafi commentators deem this hadith weak (sa'if) in its chain. Even if accepted, they interpret it as applying only when distraction (shughl) or mistake is feared due to loud voices—not absolutely. Hence the original permissibility stands.
This is a common pattern: a general prohibition is narrowed by a specific cause (takhsis bi al-sabab).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلاته إلى ظهر قاعد يتحدث) ؛ لأنه إذا رفع صوته بالحديث ربما يصير ذلك سبباً . قوله : وصلاته ؛ أي لا تكره صلاة المصلّي إلى ظهر رجل قاعد متحدّث : أي متكلم مع آخر ، وقيد القعود اتفاقي ، فإنّ الحكم لا يختلف فيما إذا كان قائماً أو مضطجعاً، وفهم من قيد التحدث أنه لو لم يكن متحدثاً لم يكره بالطريق الأولى. وفي تقييد الظهر إشارة إلى أنه يكره مواجها لوجهه ، وقد صح أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يُصلّي وعائشة رضي الله عنهم معترضة بين يديه كاعتراض الجنازة)، رواه الشيخان. وأخرج ابن أبي شيبة أن ابن عمر : كان إذا لم يجد سبيلاً إلى سارية من سواري المسجد، قال لنافع : ولّني ظهرك). وأما ما في سنن أبي داود وابن ماجه مرفوعاً: «لا تصلوا خلف النائم والمتحدث» (۳) ، فسنده ضعيف وعلى تقدير صحته فهو محمول على ما إذا خافَ الشغل والغلط برفع أصواتهم ونحوه. كذا في «العناية»، و«شرح المنية».
And his prayer towards the back of a seated person who is talking; because if he raises his voice in conversation, perhaps that might become a cause [of distraction]. He said: 'And his prayer' means: the prayer of a person praying towards the back of a seated man speaking, i.e., talking with another. The restriction of 'seated' is incidental, for the ruling does not differ whether he is standing or lying down. It is understood from the restriction of 'talking' that if he were not talking, it is even more clearly not disliked. And in restricting to the back, there is an indication that facing his face is disliked. It is authentically reported that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to pray while ‘A’ishah (may Allah be pleased with her) lay in front of him like a bier—reported by al-Bukhari and Muslim. Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated that Ibn ‘Umar, when he could not find a way to a pillar of the mosque, said to Nafi‘: 'Turn your back to me.' As for what is in Sunan Abi Dawud and Ibn Majah as marfu‘: 'Do not pray behind a sleeping or talking person,' its chain is weak, and assuming its authenticity, it is interpreted as when one fears distraction and mistake due to their raising voices and the like. Thus it is in al-‘Inayah and Sharh al-Munyah.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states that praying towards the back of a seated talking person is not disliked. The commentator clarifies that the prohibition is only when fear of distraction exists. The proof from the sunnah shows that the Prophet ﷺ prayed while ‘A’ishah lay before him, and Ibn ‘Umar instructed Nafi‘ to turn his back for him to pray towards. A seemingly contradictory hadith is weak and, if accepted, is interpreted as applying only when there is risk of disturbance. Thus the Hanafi position is that it is permissible (mubah) to pray facing someone's back, even if they are talking, as long as no distraction occurs.

Key Terms
قاعد (qa'id): A seated person; the text notes that the ruling applies whether the person is seated, standing, or lying down.
متحدث (mutahaddith): A person who is talking (speaking with another).
لا تكره (la tukrah): It is not disliked; meaning it is permissible (mubah). In Hanafi terminology, makruh tanzih is disliked but not sinful; here it is explicitly stated as not disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on praying towards the back of a seated talking person?
A) It is forbidden (haram).
B) It is disliked (makruh).
C) It is not disliked (mubah).
D) It is recommended (sunnah).

Key Takeaway
Praying towards the back of a talking person is permissible (mubah) in the Hanafi school, based on authentic hadith, as long as there is no fear of distraction.
